reported worke engliſhe hyſtorie ſaieth britayn two name called england scotland iland ocean ſea ſituate ryght ouer againſt region gallia one part iſle engliſhmen inhabite parte scottes thirde parte walſhemen fourth part corniſhmen • ther language cōditions lawes differ amonges ſelues england ſo called engliſhemen whiche winne ſame greateſt parte whiche deuided xxxix county cal shires▪ wherof britayne eaſt south wale cornewall weſt riuer twede deuideth england scotland north length iſland beginneth portſmouth ſouth part endeth twede northe conteinynge cccxx myles realm aboue moſt fruitful ſyde humbre beyōd fuller mountaines although beholder countrey far may ſeme plaen yet ful many hils thoſe moſt part voyde tree valley wherof delectable habited moſt part noble men accordynge ancient olde order deſyre dwell city nere vnto valleyes riuers ſeuerall village aduoidyng vehemēt wynds becauſe ye iland naturally ſtormy humbre hath beginnyng littell ſyde yorke runneth ſouthward holdeth courſe eaſtward ſo main ſea greatly increaſed ryuers dune trent trent beginneth little stafforde running darbyſhyre leiceſterſhyre paſſyng lichfielde notyngham right hande dune left ſo thoſe riuers make ilande called auxolme ioynyng together ſyde king ſton vpon hull goodly marchant towne fall humbre whiche riuer may aryue fraunce germanie denmarke england fruitfull beaſts aboundeth cattell wherby thinhabitauntes bee rather moſte graſiers plowman becauſe geue ſelues fedyng tyllage almoſte third part countrey imployed cattell dere redde fallow goates wherof ſtore north part cony euery ther ioly maintenance thoſe kyndes beaſtes becauſe full great woddes whereof riſeth paſtyme huntyng greatly exerciſed ſpecially nobilitie gentleman scotland part britayn purpoſe ſay nothynge becauſe haue promiſed onely briefly remembre thaffa • re myn owne countrey beſt trauailed acquainted knowlege ſame▪ wale third part britayn lyeth vpon left hand whiche like promontar • e forelande iſle euery ſide compaſſed mayne ſea except eaſt part riuer sabrine commonly called seuerne deuideth wale englande althoughe ſome late writer affirme hereford bound betwene wale englande ſaye wale beginueth chepſtoll riuer deye augmented ryuer called lugge paſſyng hereford dothe runne ſea riuer riſeth middle wale hill vncertain whether ſprynge sabrine dothe corn tacitus calleth antona euen place gothe great arme ſea paſſeth land weſtward right hand leaueth cornewall left wales▪ whiche topographye deſcription althoughe bee newe yet thoughte good ſolowe therfore wale extended town chepſtoll beginneth almoſt ſtraight line lttle aboue shroweſburye euen weſtcheſter northwarde parte ſo many britain remained alyue ſlaughter loſſe countrey lengthe dryuen ſhyftes dydde repaire ancient writynges report partely refuge mountain partly woddes marſhes remained ſafetie whiche part • enioye euen day land afterwardes englyſhmen dyd call wale britain inhabitantes ſame walſhmen amonges germains walſman ſignifieth ſtranger alien outborn ſtrange man ſuche one hathe contrary language wall tong▪ called ſtranger borne italian frencheman whiche differ ſpeche germaine man ſignifieth homo whiche man engliſhe therfore engliſhemen people germanye wonne britayne called britain whiche eſcaped deſtruction countreye countrey maner walſhemen becauſe tongue ſpeche beſides land inhabited wale name afterwardes bothe people countrey dyd remayne meanes britaines kyngdome loſt name affirm name bee deriued kynge quene without doubt deceyued coū trey ſoyle towardes ſea coaſt place valley playnes moſte fertile whiche yeldeth man beaſte great plentie fruite graſſe place moſt part bareyn leſſe fruitfull becauſe lacketh tillage cauſe huſbandmen doo lyue hardely eatynge oten cake drinkyng mylk myxt water ſowre whay ther many townes ſtrong caſteis iiii biſhoprikes biſhoprike hereforde counted englād late writer declat • firſt biſhoprike meneue ſo called meneua whiche day call sainct dauids citie ancient ſituated vppon ſea coaſt boundeth weſtward towarde irelande landaffe third bangor fourth saint aſaph vnder tharchebiſhop cantorbury walſhemen haue language thengliſhemen whiche ſaye fetche petigree frome troianes doothe partely ſound troian antiquitie partelye greeke howe ſo euer walſhemen pronounce ſpeache ſo pleaſauntly gentilly thenglyſhemen doo becauſe ſpeake throte contrarywyſe thengliſhemen rightly folowyng latines doo expreſſe voyce ſomwhat within lyps hearer ſemeth pleaſant ſweete thus much wale third part britain foloweth fourth laſte part britayne named cornewall part beginneth ſyde ſtandeth towarde spayne weſtward toward eaſt bredth iiii ſcore ten mile extending little beyonde ſaint germains whiche famous village ſituated ryghte hand vppon ſea coaſte greateſt breadth countrey xx myles parcell lande right hand cō paſſed coaſt mayn ſea left hand arme ſea declared parteth land runneth vp chepſtoll countrey fourme horne fyrſt narowe groweth broader little beyonde ſaid towne ſaint germayne eaſtward bordreth vpon england weſt ſouth north mayn ſea round bareyn ſoyle yeldynge fruite trauaile tyllers huſbandmen goodneſſe grounde greate plentie leade tynne mynyng diggyng wherof doth ſpecially conſyſt liuynge ſuſtentation inhabitantes onely partt britayn euen day continueth nation britain ye beginnyng brought gallia occupied habited iland credite may geuen whiche reporte firſt inhabitantes britayn come city armerica argumēt profe wherof becauſe corniſhemen doo ſpeake language britain vſe france whō briton doo call britonantes thing true old ancient chronicle doth declare wherin foūd written cornubia cornugallia compounded cornu horne forme wherof countrey hath gallia oute countrey thinhabitants came firſt maner name miſlyked tongue farr diſſonant engliſh muche lyke walſhe tongue becauſe haue many word cōmune tonges yet difference betweene walſhman ſpeaketh cornyſheman rather vnderſtandeth many wordes ſpoken walſhman whole tale telleth whereby manyfeſte thoſe thre people vnderſtand one lyke maner southerne scot doo perceiue vnderſtand northern thyng rare meruailous one iland ſhould ſuch varietie ſpeches cornewall cornugall dioceſſe excetour whiche one worthy counted fourth part ilād wel contrarietie language firſt inhabitant thereof beforeſaid afterwardes normains whiche conſtituted kyngdom thoſe thre partes reckened cornewall one county ſhires countrey thus much particular deſcription britayne whole body realme membres may better knowen ſome peraduenture neuer heard ſame forme ilande triquetra thre cornered hauyng thre corner thre ſides two wherof ſay corner toward theaſt thother toward weſte • bothe extendyng northward ar longeſt third ſyde ſouth ſyde • • ſhorter thother iland
